S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Room-Temperature Stationary Sodium-Ion Batteries for Large-Scale Electric Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2338</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2360</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ee40847g</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D2338-2360%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BPan%26author%3DY.%2BS.%2BHu%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DRoom-Temperature%2BStationary%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bfor%2BLarge-Scale%2BElectric%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ee40847g&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b09496&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ee40847g&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2338-2360</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liNJByFRKrpxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisrzJ&amp;md5=2e02460553edc21e1ea8b73982ed63bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.  After further in-depth exploration and investigation, we believe that Na-ion batteries are promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB4Pf2vZ5QrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgom0OMyr_YoA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFelsrnN&amp;md5=8311789a2dc4e61dabff177245235c3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA06467D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent developments in electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Luyuan Paul; Yu, Linghui; Wang, Xin; Srinivasan, Madhavi; Xu, Zhichuan J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The rapid consumption of nonrenewable resources resulted in an ever-increasing problem of CO2 emissions that has motivated people for studying the harvesting of energy from renewable alternatives (e.g. solar and wind).  Efficient electrochem. energy storage devices play a crucial role in storing harvested energies in the daily lives.  For example, rechargeable batteries can store energy generated by solar cells during the daytime and release it during night-time.  In particular, Li-ion batteries (LIBs) have received considerable attention ever since their early commercialization in 1990s.  However, with initiatives by several governments to build large-scale energy grids to store energy for cities, problems such as the high cost and limited availability of Li starts to become major issues.  Na, which also belongs to Group 1 of the periodic table, has comparable electrochem. properties to Li, and more importantly it is considerably more accessible than Li.  Nonetheless, research into Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is currently still in its infancy compared to LIBs, although great leaps and bounds have been made recently in terms of research and development into this technol.  Here in this review, the authors summarize the recent advancements made, also covering the prospective materials for both the battery cathode and anode.  Addnl., opinions on possible solns. through correlating trends in recent papers will be suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqaYAOgglkaCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfccuzwxNAUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjs1yhsbo%253D&amp;md5=95489f575e9ded7e312db8576036b208</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1149/2.0091514jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Irisarri, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ponrouch, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palacin, M.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Slater, Michael D.; Kim, Donghan; Lee, Eungje; Doeff, Marca; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are currently emerging as a replacement for lithium ion batteries due to sodium abundance in the earth's crust.  The recent development of sodium ion batteries anode has been achieved by the use of selected carbon as an anode.  The performance of the selected carbon materials such as the charge/discharge capacity, voltage profile and cyclic stability, depend strongly on the sizes, additives, electrolytes and structures.  Based on the contribution of the carbon-based materials as a replacement of the sodium ion batteries anode, much improvement has been achieved.  However, more investigations are still required in order to identify the suitable carbon materials that can provide and improve the anode properties.  In the same vein, alloy materials have gained increasing effort as high capacity anode and their combination with carbon have contributed to the development of sodium ion batteries.  In this review, we have accounted for the development of carbon-based materials and their composites with alloy materials as well as their prospects and challenges for sodium ion battery anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLqTy97T_9sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgKbFfoo5UMdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOmsbvM&amp;md5=5bc4c118e6be905d663496bf2953e8d7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201402511"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ha, K.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Towards more sustainable negative electrodes in Na-ion batteries via nanostructured iron oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Valvo, M.; Lindgren, F.; Lafont, U.; Bjoerefors, F.; Edstroem, K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion technol. could emerge as an alternative to Li-ion batteries due to limited costs and vast availability of sodium, as well as its similar chem.  Several Na-rich compds. were proposed as pos. electrodes, whereas suitable neg. counterparts were not found yet.  Nanostructured iron oxide is reported here for the 1st time as a potentially viable neg. electrode for Na-ion cells based on conventional electrolytes and composite coatings with CM-cellulose.  Electrochem. reactions of Na+ and Li+ ions with nanostructured Fe2O3 are analyzed and compared.  Initial sodiation of Fe2O3 yields a sloping profile in a voltage range characteristic for oxide conversion, which instead generates a typical plateau upon lithiation.  Application of such earth-abundant, nontoxic material in upcoming Na-ion batteries is potentially groundbreaking, since it offers important advantages, namely: i. simple and cost-effective synthesis of Fe2O3 nanostructures at low temps.; ii. cheaper and more sustainable cell fabrication with higher energy densities, e.g., use of natural, water-sol. binders, as well as Al for both current collectors; iii. electrochem. performances with specific gravimetric capacities exceeding 400 mAh g-1 at 40 mA g-1, accompanied by decent sp. vol. energy densities, e.g., ≈1.22 Wh cm-3, provided that cycle inefficiencies and long-term durability are addressed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMUA0bO_kCk7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljSsm0Is1ggSw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Rich Mesoporous Carbon as Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Sun, Ning; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Zhu, Qizhen; Wu, Feng; Qiao, Ning; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

The XPS anal. indicates that the carbon has a high nitrogen content of 7.78 at.%, in the forms of pyridinic and pyrrolic, as well as graphitic nitrogen. The excellent sodium storage performance of the nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon is attributed to its disordered structure with large interlayer distance, interconnected porosity, and the enriched nitrogen heteroatoms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwkJbCuGMkELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljSsm0Is1ggSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOrtr3M&amp;md5=26b08a49898c6e6ae937f4de90e676f6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA05118E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of High Performance Hard Carbon Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A highly reversible, resource-abundant and low-cost anode is indispensable to the future success of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) in large-scale energy storage application.  The authors report the facile synthesis of a biomass-derived hard carbon for SIBs by 1-step pyrolysis of shaddock peel under an inert atm. without activation or any further treatments.  The pyrolytic carbon shows very high reversible sodium storage capacities up to 430.5 mA h/g at a c.d. of 30 mA/g and superior cycling stability with only 2.5% capacity loss over 200 charge-discharge cycles. The good Na-ion storage property of the shaddock peel-derived pyrolytic carbon is attributed to its unique honeycomb-like morphol. with a shortened distance for Na-ion diffusion, and the large interlayer distance which is available for sodium insertion/extn.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrUZb0nR_lduLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljSsm0Is1ggSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVegtr7O&amp;md5=32487f69bba862d984793316e10ff8e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.04.040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lv, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-doped Carbon/Graphene Hybrid Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Excellent Rate Capability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon nanoparticles as high-capacity, high-stability anodic materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Lifen; Cao, Yuliang; Henderson, Wesley A.; Sushko, Maria L.; Shao, Yuyan; Xiao, Jie; Wang, Wei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Nie, Zimin; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

                10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00114</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D48%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D1657-1665%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BDing%26author%3DD.%2BMitlin%26title%3DTin%2Band%2BTin%2BCompounds%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BAnodes%253A%2BPhase%2BTransformations%2Band%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.5b00114&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b09496&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.5b00114&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin and Tin Compounds for Sodium Ion Battery Anodes: Phase Transformations and Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhi; Ding, Jia; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1657-1665</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium ion batteries (NIB, NAB, SIB) are attracting interest as a potentially lower cost alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIB), with readily available and geog. democratic reserves of the metal.  Tin is one of most promising SIB anode materials, which alloys with up to 3.75 Na, leading to a charge storage capacity of 847 mAh g-1.  In this Account, we outline the state-of-the-art understanding regarding the sodiation-induced phase transformations and the assocd. performance in a range of Sn-based systems, treating metallic Sn and its alloys, tin oxide (SnO2), tin sulfide (SnS2/SnS), and tin phosphide (Sn4P3).  We first detail what is known about the sodiation sequence in metallic Sn, highlighting the most recent insight into the reactions prior to the terminal equil. Na15Sn4 intermetallic.  We explain why researchers argue that the equil. (phase diagram) series of phase transitions does not occur in this system, and rather why sodiation/desodiation proceeds through a series of metastable cryst. and amorphous structures.  We also outline the recent modeling-based insight regarding how this phase transition profoundly influences the mech. properties of the alloy, progressively changing the bonding and the near neighbor arrangement from "Sn-like" to "Na-like" in the process.  We then go on to discuss the sodiation reactions in SnO2.  We argue that while a substantial amt. of exptl. work already exists where the focus is on synthesis and testing of tin oxide-based nanocomposites, the exact sodiation sequence is just beginning to be understood.  Unlike in Sn and Sn alloys, where capacities near the theor. are reached at least early during cycling, SnO2 never quite achieves anything close to the 1398 mAh g-1 that would be possible with a combination of fully reversible conversion and alloying reactions.  We highlight recent work demonstrating that contrary to general expectations, it is the Sn to Na15Sn4 alloying reaction that is incomplete and hence limits the capacity of the electrode.  We also describe how the oxide conversion reaction goes through an intermediate SnO phase, and how its reversibility in a half-cell is highly dependent on the terminal anodic voltage.  We then present what is known about sodiation of tin sulfide and of tin phosphide phases, including emerging microstructural evidence that may explain why both the sulfides and the phosphides are unable to achieve their highly promising theor. capacities under conventional electrode testing conditions.  Finally, we provide a broad comparison of the capacity (cycling and rate) performance for a range of Sn based anode materials, and show that there may be indeed an optimum microstructural architecture.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGraHWeuL6zqAbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgNVbSklFdzEw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensionally interconnected nickel-antimony intermetallic hollow nanospheres as anode material for high-rate sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jun; Yang, Zhenzhong; Wang, Jiaqing; Gu, Lin; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

The 3D interconnected hollow structure and Ni matrix encapsulation contribute significantly to the excellent structure stability and high electrochem. performance of the Sb-based anode.  They exhibit highly stable and substantial discharge capacities of 400, 372, 230 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles at 1C, 5C, 10C, resp.  Moreover, a full Na0.4Mn0.54Co0.46O2//NiSb battery shows at a c.d. of 300 mA/gSb a charge and discharge capacity of 451 and 301 mA h g-1, resp., and also displayed relatively good stability, retaining 75% of the initial discharge capacity after 20 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGopuy1h1ajWGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgNVbSklFdzEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht12gtLfN&amp;md5=689f7b6f69d04607f28778b9a31bf92c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.02.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, Z.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical nanotubes assembled from MoS2-carbon monolayer sandwiched superstructure nanosheets for high-performance sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Zheng-Tian; Kang, Wenpei; Xu, Jun; Sun, Yi-Wen; Jiang, Miao; Ng, Tsz-Wai; Xue, Hong-Tao; Yu, Denis Y. W.; Zhang, Wenjun; Lee, Chun-Sing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">27-37</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Interface engineering on 2D layered nanomaterials plays pivotal roles in achieving novel properties and superior device performance.  In this work, hierarchical nanotubes consisting of 2D monolayer MoS2 and carbon (MoS2:C) interoverlapped superstructure nanosheets have been synthesized, in which the MoS2 and carbon layers are alternately sandwiched.  The hierarchical architectures assembled from the MoS2:C superstructures are beneficial for: (i) providing substantially expanded (002) interlayer spacing (0.98 nm) of 2H-MoS2 which facilitates fast Na+ insertion/extn. reaction kinetics, (ii) improving elec. cond. of MoS2 by carbon monolayer insertion with ideal heterointerface contact, (iii) preventing aggregation of MoS2 nanosheets, and (iv) accommodating vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  The superstructure nanotubes are demonstrated as a robust anode material for sodium storage with superior electrochem. performance.  They deliver a high rate-capability and maintain discharge capacities of 295 and 187 mAh g-1 at high current densities of 10.0 and 20.0 A g-1, resp.  Furthermore, they show durable cycling life (capacity retention of 101.3%, 108.2% and 107.8% after 200 cycles at current densities of 0.2, 0.5 and 1.0 A g-1, resp., in comparison to those of the 2nd cycles), and an initial Coulombic efficiency as high as 84%.  The MoS2:C superstructure nanotubes perform among the best of current MoS2-based electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqPqvqO_ClQJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0libAe9qn0b2ow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitlGju7w%253D&amp;md5=250b77306f2bd58ddc6f89017d5b9702</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA01963J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jahel, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ghimbeu, C.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exceptionally highly performing Na-ion battery anode using crystalline SnO2 nanoparticles confined in mesoporous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jahel, Ali; Ghimbeu, Camelia Matei; Darwiche, Ali; Vidal, Loic; Hajjar-Garreau, Samar; Vix-Guterl, Cathie; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11960-11969</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Confined and unconfined SnO2 nanoparticles in the pores of mesoporous carbon were prepd. and tested as anode materials vs. Na.  Both composites present small cryst. SnO2 particles (∼3 nm) but different location and dispersion in the carbon matrix.  When the particles are homogeneously distributed and confined in the carbon pores, an initial reversible capacity of 780 mA h g-1 is achieved with unprecedented capacity retention of 80 and 54% after 100 and 4000 cycles, resp., at a high current rate (50 C, 1800 mA g-1).  Unexpectedly, over two current rate variation cycles from 1 C to 500 C, the composite recovers 81% and 97%, resp. after returning from the 500 C to the 1 C rate.  To our knowledge, no other material with such a long cycling life and superior performance in terms of capacity and rate capability has been reported so far for sodium ion batteries.  HRTEM, XRD, N2 adsorption, XPS and galvanostatic cycling results suggest that confined SnO2 particles undergo an enhanced sodium alloying/dealloying process due to their special confinement inside the pores, which increases their cond., facilitates the diffusion of Na+ ions and buffers the large volumetric changes during charge/discharge.  These high performances cannot be delivered when SnO2 is not confined and not well dispersed in the carbon pores.  This work demonstrates that nano-confinement of anode species in carbon is a valuable concept affording the modification of the fundamental properties of guest species along with their electrochem. performances leading to highly stable and performing materials with a long life for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmSgtWPTSt8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0libAe9qn0b2ow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFGgur4%253D&amp;md5=219ee2777f1e53956a82fdbab173128f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/nl403053v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simply mixed commercial red phosphorus and carbon nanotube composite with exceptionally reversible sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been given intense attention because they are the most promising alternative to lithium ion batteries for application in renewable power stations and smart grid, owing to their low cost, their abundant natural resources, and the similar chem. of sodium and lithium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is the most promising anode materials for SIBs with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, but the com. available red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly.  Here, we report that simply hand-grinding com. microsized red phosphorus and carbon nanotubes (CNTs) can deliver a reversible capacity of 1675 mA h g-1 for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), with capacity retention of 76.6% over 10 cycles.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomass derived hard carbon used as a high performance anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Kun-lei; Long, Qie; Zeng, Rui; Yi, Zi-qi; Zhang, Wei; Wang, Duo; Yin, Wei; Wu, Chao; Fan, Qing-jie; Zhang, Wu-xing; Huang, Yun-hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A porous hard carbon material was synthesized by the simple pyrolysis of H3PO4-treated biomass, i.e., pomelo peels, at 700 °C in N2.  The as-obtained hard carbon had a 3D connected porous structure and a large sp. surface area of 1272 m2 g-1.  XPS anal. showed that the carbon material was functionalized by O-contg. and P-contg. groups.  The porous hard carbon was used as an anode for sodium ion batteries and exhibited good cycling stability and rate capability, delivering a capacity of 181 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 220 cycles and retaining a capacity of 71 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical Insertion of Li and Na Ions into Nanocrystalline Fe3O4 and α-Fe2O3 for Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Komaba, Shinichi; Mikumo, Takashi; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Ogata, Atsushi; Yoshida, Hiromi; Yamada, Yasuhiro</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

The electrochem. activity was significantly enhanced as the mean particle size decreased.  The nanocrystd. Fe3O4 (10 nm) prepd. by pptn. method delivered 190 mA-h/g of the rechargeable capacity in the voltage range of 2-3 V in a lithium-ion contg. electrolyte, whereas the 400 and 100 nm Fe3O4 powders showed 10 and 80 mA-h/g of the rechargeable capacity, resp.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A rationally designed dual role anode material for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries: case study of eco-friendly Fe3O4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hariharan, Srirama; Saravanan, Kuppan; Ramar, Vishwanathan; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Identifying dual role electrode materials capable of storing both lithium and sodium are thought to be highly relevant, as these materials could find potential applications simultaneously in lithium- and sodium-ion batteries.  In this regard, the concept of dual alkali storage is demonstrated in Fe3O4 anode material undergoing conversion reaction.  To enable improved storage, a rational active material and electrode design is proposed.  Accordingly, the following features were simultaneously incorporated into the design: (a) an optimal particle size, (b) a conducting matrix, (c) adequately large active material surface area and (d) strong electrode material-current collector integrity.  Electrodes incorporating this rational design exhibit excellent high-rate performance and impressive cyclability during lithium storage.  For instance, Fe3O4 electrodes deliver a charge capacity of 950 mA-h/g at 1.2C (∼2.6 times higher than graphite and 5.4 times higher than Li4Ti5O12).  Further, these electrodes show no signs of capacity fade even up to 1100 cycles.  Impressively, the cells could also be charged-discharged to 65% of their theor. capacity in just 5 min or 12C (11.11 A/g).  The rate performance and cyclability of lithium storage achieved here are amongst the highest reported values in the literature for the conversion reaction in Fe3O4.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A facile synthesis of Fe3O4 nanoparticles/graphene for high-performance lithium/sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fu, Yanqing; Wei, Qiliang; Wang, Xianyou; Zhang, Gaixia; Shu, Hongbo; Yang, Xiukang; Tavares, Ana C.; Sun, Shuhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A type of porous carbon-Fe3O4 (e.g., PC-Fe3O4) composite with an industrially scalable prodn. was introduced in the sodium ion battery application for the first time.  The PC-Fe3O4 composite, consisting of highly dispersed Fe3O4 nanocrystals within the porous carbon with a relatively low wt. percent of 45.5 wt%, could efficiently demonstrate high capacities of 225, 168, 127, 103, 98 and 90 mA h g-1 under the current densities of 50, 100, 200, 300, 400 and 500 mA g-1 with a good stability over 400 cycles. More importantly, a new concept of an elemental iron-based sodium ion battery of PC-Fe3O4/Na2FeP2O7 is presented.  This is the first example to introduce an element-rich configuration in the sodium ion battery from the viewpoint of sustainability.  The full battery demonstrated a superior capacity of 93 mA h g-1, high capacity retention of 93.3% over 100 cycles and work voltage around 2.28 V with the energy d. of 203 W h kg-1.  Such configuration of an iron-based sodium battery would be highly promising and sustainable owing to its low cost and high stability in grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlfLDULELEl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXN8TYDsbL2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFehtb7J&amp;md5=dbdb474ad5240a7412c37b8740147f9c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA01836J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qi, L.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zuo, Z.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xin, Y.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, C.-K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.-H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Quantization of FerroferricOxide Embedded in 3D Microcarbon for Ultrahigh Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ quantization of ferroferric oxide embedded in 3D microcarbon for ultrahigh performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qi, Li-Ya; Zhang, Yi-Wei; Zuo, Zi-Cheng; Xin, Yue-Long; Yang, Cheng-Kai; Wu, Bin; Zhang, Xin-Xiang; Zhou, Heng-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Unlike conventional carbon coating strategies which only focus on the macrodimension to enhance elec. cond. and alleviate vol. variation for high-capacity metal oxide anode materials, a hierarchically raspberry-like microstructure embedded with three-dimensional carbon-coated Fe3O4 quantum dots is built for ultrafast rechargeable sodium ion batteries.  Taking advantage of using metal org. frameworks (MOFs) as templates, it realizes an in situ quantization process in which Fe3O4 quantum dots are formed and uniformly embedded in microcarbon coating protection.  Due to the short diffusion length and integrated hierarchical conductive network, the electrode combines supercapacitor-like rate performance (e.g., less than 6 min to full charge/discharge) and battery-like capacity (e.g., maintaining &gt;90% of theor. capacity).  An interesting surface-induced process which imitates pseudocapacitive behaviors in supercapacitors is analyzed in detail.  This proof-of-concept study and insightful understanding on sodium storage in this investigation may inherently solve the widely encountered problems existing in high-capacity metal oxide anode materials and point out new directions for the future development of ultrafast rechargeable sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqjWmm31SJIIrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXN8TYDsbL2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xms1Wit78%253D&amp;md5=4acdbd55c6027747f8f18818aac8d594</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.02.097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Reduced Graphene Oxides Hydrogel Anchored with Ultrafine CoO Nanoparticles as Anode for Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Reduced Graphene Oxides Hydrogel Anchored with Ultrafine CoO Nanoparticles as Anode for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Mei; Wang, Yu; Jia, Mengqiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional reduced graphene oxides hydrogel anchored with ultrafine CoO nanoparticles (CoO/RGO nanocomposite) was prepd. by a facile hydrothermal strategy and subsequently heat-treatment process.  The small-size CoO nanoparticles are encapsulated within graphene-based hydrogel with robust interconnected networks for the CoO/RGO nanocomposite.  The electrochem. performances are evaluated by using coin-type cells.  It delivers high rate capacities of 890.2, 690.4, 543.8 and 457.0 mAh g-1, even at 200, 800, 1600 and 2400 mA g-1, resp.  The specific capacity increases to 1025.8 mAh g-1 after 82 cycles when the c.d. is back to 100 mA g-1, indicating excellent rate capability and cycle stability.  The improved electrochem. performance is ascribed to the fabricated structure with three-dimensional RGO nanosheets.  The CoO/RGO nanocomposite will be a promising candidate of anode material for Li ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8gQE4TcYW_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXN8TYDsbL2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmslejtrY%253D&amp;md5=3e4b6c8adeea23b773d898f9835ae0c1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201301928"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duan, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Functionalized Graphene Hydrogel-Based High-Performance Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Functionalized Graphene Hydrogel-Based High-Performance Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Yuxi; Lin, Zhaoyang; Huang, Xiaoqing; Wang, Yang; Huang, Yu; Duan, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A convenient one-step strategy is presented to prep. functionalized graphene hydrogels (FGHs) incorporating hydroquinones into the high-surface-area 3D graphene framework via k-k interaction as a pseudocapacitive component.  This methodol. allows efficient loading of pseudocapacitive hydroquinone mols. and fast charge transfer between graphene and hydroquinone, as well as ensuring rapid ion diffusion and electron transport throughout the porous network.  The as-prepd. FGHs exhibit outstanding electrochem. performance, including ultrahigh specific capacitances and excellent cycling stability in the aq. electrolyte.  The mech. strong FGHs have been further assembled into flexible solid-state supercapacitors using H2SO4-PVA gel as the electrolyte.  The as-fabricated devices show superior capacitive performance and exceptional mech. flexibility.  These results reveal that the electrochem. performances of graphene-based electrodes can be promoted by combination of surface functionalization and hierarchical structures of graphene sheets.  This study demonstrates a pathway to the rational design and fabrication of functionalized 3D graphene materials for electrochem. energy storage and flexible electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_-hHn6Xtw3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhD23Uu9xrmoQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1Sku7fM&amp;md5=28cc2aacd58d0dd43cf0fcad8a5d156e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2015.01.062"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yung, K.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Green and facile synthesis of Fe3O4 and graphene nanocomposites with enhanced rate capability and cycling stability for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yucheng; Zhang, Zhenyu; Xia, Yang; Chui, Ying-San; Lee, Jong-Min; Zapien, Juan Antonio</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of graphene@Fe3O4@C core-shell nanosheets for high-performance lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zehui; Wang, Fei; An, Qiao; Li, Wei; Wu, Peiyi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7036-7043</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of anode materials with high capacity and long cycle life, while maintaining low prodn. cost is crucial for achieving high-performance Li-ion batteries (LIBs).  Herein, the authors report a simple and cost-effective 1-pot solvothermal method to synthesize graphene@Fe3O4@C core-shell nanosheets as a LIB anode with improved electrochem. performance.  In this case, ferrocene was used as the precursor for both Fe3O4 and C, while graphene oxide was used as a template for the resultant 2-dimensional nanostructure and conductive graphene backbone.  The obtained graphene@Fe3O4@C core-shell nanosheets have a unique core-shell nanostructure, ultra-small Fe3O4 nanoparticles (∼6 nm), and a high surface area of ∼136 m2 g-1 show a high reversible capacity of ∼1468 mA h g-1, an excellent rate capability and long cycle life, which reflects the ability of graphene backbone to enhance the cond. and C coating to prevent agglomeration of Fe oxide nanoparticles.  These findings provide a new approach to the design and synthesis of high-performance anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpnlExk9lrBjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhD23Uu9xrmoQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXisVygsb8%253D&amp;md5=ab782ad9776c55c688aff86993e5734f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/C4RA09079A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-step solvothermal preparation of Fe3O4/graphene composites at elevated temperature and their application as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Laiying; Fu, Aiping; Li, Hongliang; Liu, Jingquan; Guo, Peizhi; Wang, Yiqian; Zhao, Xiu Song</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">104</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">59981-59989</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A one-step high-temp. solvothermal process (can be used up to 400 °C) has been explored for the prepn. of Fe3O4/graphene composites.  The influence of high temp. (&gt;230 °C) on the structure, morphol. and electrochem. properties of the resulting Fe3O4/graphene composites was investigated by XRD, SEM, TEM and N2 adsorption-desorption measurements.  Electrochem. performances of the as-prepd. Fe3O4/graphene composites at different temps. were evaluated in coin-type cells as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  In comparison with the traditional solvothermal method (&lt;240 °C), the high-temp. method does not require an addnl. calcination process yet it still could result in Fe3O4/graphene composites with pure phase and excellent electrochem. properties.  A preferred solvothermal temp. of 280 °C has been deduced based on a series of control expts.  The Fe3O4/graphene composite derived at 280 °C exhibited a high reversible capacity of 907 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C (92.6 mA g-1) even after 65 cycles, showing outstanding cycle stability.  It also exhibited a high rate capability of 410 mA h g-1 at 2 C (1852 mA g-1).  The role of the graphene substrates in improving the electrochem. properties of the composite is discussed based on the morphol., structure, phase and electrochem. property studies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodveIuK-fJGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhD23Uu9xrmoQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVGhs7fO&amp;md5=95062f102245c7c4a7e8513755ed9f4f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms12122"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chao, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Savilov, S.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Array of nanosheets render ultrafast and high-capacity Na-ion storage by tunable pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Yang, Peihua; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Wang, Jin; Fan, Xiaofeng; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Fan, Hong Jin; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a potentially low-cost and safe alternative to the prevailing lithium-ion battery technol.  However, it is a great challenge to achieve fast charging and high power d. for most sodium-ion electrodes because of the sluggish sodiation kinetics.  Here we demonstrate a high-capacity and high-rate sodium-ion anode based on ultrathin layered tin(II) sulfide nanostructures, in which a maximized extrinsic pseudocapacitance contribution is identified and verified by kinetics anal.  The graphene foam supported tin(II) sulfide nanoarray anode delivers a high reversible capacity of ∼1,100 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 and ∼420 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1, which even outperforms its lithium-ion storage performance.  The surface-dominated redox reaction rendered by our tailored ultrathin tin(II) sulfide nanostructures may also work in other layered materials for high-performance sodium-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVSw-KQ43s-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgmBEIYMmqv4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFSqtLbO&amp;md5=3f7ab452279e7159794a832183e58387</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/nl504038s"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chao, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, Z.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene Quantum Dots Coated VO2 Arrays for Highly Durable Electrodes for Li and Na Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Zhang, Xiao; Wang, Jin; Liang, Pei; Lin, Jianyi; Zhang, Hua; Shen, Ze Xiang; Fan, Hong Jin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanoscale surface engineering is playing important role in enhancing the performance of battery electrode.  VO2 is one of high-capacity but less-stable materials and has been used mostly in the form of powders for Li-ion battery cathode with mediocre performance.  In this work, we design a new type of binder-free cathode by bottom-up growth of bifacial VO2 arrays directly on a graphene network for both high-performance Li-ion and Na-ion battery cathodes.  More importantly, graphene quantum dots are coated onto the VO2 surfaces as a highly efficient surface sensitizer and protection to further boost the electrochem. properties.  The integrated electrodes deliver a Na storage capacity of 306 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g, and a capacity of more than 110 mA-h/g after 1500 cycles at 18 A/g.  Our result on Na-ion battery may pave the way to next generation post-lithium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlNChWsQ5gnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgmBEIYMmqv4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFehsL7L&amp;md5=64c5ad4c1680e984a714a38620297d09</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.03.139"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, J.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, D.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, C.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.-H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Li and Na Storage Behavior of Bowl-Like Hollow Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Microspheres as an Anode Material for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li and Na storage behavior of bowl-like hollow Co3O4 microspheres as an anode material for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Jian-Wu; Zhang, Da-Wei; Zang, Yong; Sun, Xin; Cheng, Bin; Ding, Chu-Xiong; Yu, Yan; Chen, Chun-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">132</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">193-199</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bowl-like hollow Co3O4 microspheres are prepd. via a simple and low-cost route by thermally treating Co-contg. resorcinol-formaldehyde composites gel in air.  SEM, transmission electron microscope and N2 adsorption-desorption measurements demonstrate that these bowl-like hollow Co3O4 microspheres are composed of hollow inner cavities and outer shell walls (70 nm thickness), on which a considerable amt. of mesopores centered around 5-17 nm size are distributed.  When employed as the anode material for lithium-ion batteries, these bowl-like hollow Co3O4 microspheres exhibit extraordinary cycling performance (111% retention after 50 cycles owing to capacity rise), fairly high rate capacity (650 mAh g-1 at 5 C) and enhanced lithium storage capacity.  Meanwhile, the Na-storage behavior of Co3O4 as an anode material of Na-ion batteries is initially investigated based on such a hollow structure and it exhibits similar feature of discharge/charge profiles and a high initial discharge capacity but relatively moderate capacity retention compared with the Li-storage performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpAgeumO-nSj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgmBEIYMmqv4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXos1egu7k%253D&amp;md5=edf48f4ad7673d72aaf2e2304bc22426</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C3CC47977C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>Nanocrystals Anchored onto GrapheneNanosheets as the Anode Material for Low-Cost Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/am502424j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, D. Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Myung, S. T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-Coated Magnetite Embedded on Carbon Nanotubes for Rechargeable Lithium and Sodium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.
